## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics / nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form for driven/damped nonlinear oscillators. Common models include linear harmonic motion, nonlinear restoring forces (Duffing-type), and nonlinear damping/self-excitation (Van der Pol/Rayleigh), often with periodic forcing or parametric modulation in time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (small-amplitude, conservative spring-like restoring acceleration; sign captured by c0)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped linear oscillator in first-order form)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Nonlinear restoring (cubic/Duffing backbone): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (stiffening/softening spring)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance, jump phenomena)
- Quintic restoring extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger nonlinearity at larger |x|)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic/cubic drag): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag in 1D)
- Van der Pol form (self-excited via negative damping near origin): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (limit-cycle oscillator; sign pattern learned via constants)
- Rayleigh form (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * v**2) * v (nonlinear damping creating limit cycles)
- Parametric stiffness modulation: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric excitation)
- Nonlinear parametric Duffing: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * x**3 + c4 * v (parametrically driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Saturating restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * x) + c2 * v (soft-limited restoring acceleration)
- Amplitude-dependent frequency surrogate (mixed terms): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * v**2 + c3 * v (captures effective stiffness changes coupled to kinetic energy)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (and not explicitly on t), suggesting a restoring force derived from a potential U(x) (e.g., polynomial in x).
- Odd symmetry in x (dv_dt ≈ -f(x) with f odd) indicates symmetric potentials (U even), typical for centered springs; even-powered x terms in dv_dt suggest asymmetry/bias.
- Pure viscous damping appears as a term proportional to v; nonlinear damping often appears as v*Abs(v) or v**3, producing stronger dissipation at high speed.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior is often captured by damping that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c0 + c1*x**2)*v or (c0 + c1*v**2)*v.
- External periodic drive typically enters additively as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t); presence of harmonics (sin(2*c*t), etc.) suggests nonlinear forcing or waveform distortion.
- Parametric excitation is indicated by time-periodic coefficients multiplying x (or v), e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, leading to Mathieu-like instability tongues.
- Hardening/softening spring behavior is reflected by positive/negative cubic stiffness terms (x**3) affecting resonance frequency with amplitude.
- If dv_dt includes mixed terms like x*v or x*v**2, it can indicate geometric or inertial nonlinearities (state-dependent effective stiffness/damping).
- Soft-limiting mechanisms (impacts/stops or saturating springs) often fit better with bounded nonlinearities like tanh(c*x) rather than high-degree polynomials.

GT: -mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x**c5
Candidate formulas: 51

GT (fixed) is
\[
-0.4316737116\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;1.4716230087\,x^3\;-\;1.4716230087\,x(0.0306959168\,t+1).
\]
Rewrite to expose required term types:
\[
(-0.4316737116)v \;+\; (0.4316737116)\,v x^2 \;+\; (-1.4716230087)x^3 \;+\; (-1.4716230087)x \;+\; (-1.4716230087\cdot 0.0306959168)\,t x.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly** these five monomials: \(v\), \(v x^2\), \(x^3\), \(x\), and \(t x\), with **no other functional dependence** (no \(e^{kt}\), no trig in \(t\), no rational-in-\(x\), etc.). In particular, the \(t x\) term is *linear in \(t\)*, not exponential/trigonometric.

Now check candidates:

1. Has \(v, x^3, v x^2\) but the \(x\)-with-\(t\) part is \(x e^{c4 t}\) plus extra rational and cosine terms. \(x e^{c4 t}\) cannot equal \(x(\alpha t+\beta)\) for all \(t\). Setting \(c4=0\) makes it constant-in-\(t\), still no \(t x\). **No**.

2. Same issue: \(x e^{c4 t}\) cannot produce \(t x\). **No**.

3. Pure polynomials plus \(x e^{c8 t}\); cannot make \(t x\). **No**.

4. Same: \(x e^{c4 t}\) cannot become \(t x\). **No**.

5. Has \(x e^{c7 t}\) and \(x e^{c5 x^2}\); neither can produce \(t x\) globally. **No**.

6. Has \(x e^{c4 t}\) and rational terms; cannot produce \(t x\). **No**.

9. Has \(x^{c8} e^{c9 t}\); again exponential in \(t\). **No**.

10. Has \(x\sin(c5 t+c6)\); sinusoid cannot equal linear \(t\) for all \(t\). Phase shifts don’t help (still bounded periodic). **No**.

11. Has constant term \(c2\) and sinusoidal \(x^{c6}\sin(\cdot)\); cannot match required \(t x\) and also GT has no standalone constant. **No**.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO29)

GT: -mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x**c5
Candidates evaluated: 51
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.431673711555058*v*(1 - x**2) - 1.47162300874852*x**3 - 1.47162300874852*x*(0.0306959168053925*t + 1)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.431673711555058*v + 0.431673711555058*v*x**2 - 1.47162300874852*x**3 - 0.0451752948498613*x*t - 1.47162300874852*x`

So GT = `-0.431674*v + 0.431674*v*x² - 1.47162*x³ - 1.47162*x - 0.04518*x*t`

The basis functions in GT are: **v, v·x², x³, x, x·t**

The key question for each candidate is whether it can represent the term `x·t` (linear in both x and t).

Let me check which candidates can produce an `x·t` term. The term `x·t` can potentially come from:
- `x*exp(c*t)` — NO, this is exponential, not linear in t
- `x*cos(c*t)` or `x*sin(c*t+c)` — NO, these are periodic, not linear
- `x*t` directly — only if explicitly present

None of the candidates have an explicit `x*t` term. So I need to check if any candidate's functional form can exactly reproduce `x*t` through some combination.

**Critical check:** Can `x*exp(c4*t)` produce `x*t`? No — exponentials cannot equal linear functions for all t. Can `x*cos(c*t)` produce `x*t`? No. Can `x*sin(c*t + c)` produce `x*t`? No.

Can any rational function of x produce `x*t`? No, since t doesn't appear in rational functions of x.

Let me check if `x*exp(c*t)` with c→0 gives just `x` (constant), not `x*t`. Setting c4=0 gives `c3*x`, which is just a constant times x, not x*t.

**None of the candidates can produce the `x*t` term exactly.** The GT requires a term linear in both x and t, and no candidate provides this basis function.

Let me verify each candidate systematically — every candidate uses either `exp(c*t)`, `cos(c*t)`, `sin(c*t+c)`, or `x^c * exp(c*t)` to capture t-dependence. None of these can exactly equal `c*x*t` for all t.

For candidates with `x^c * exp(c*t)` (like Candidate 7 with `c4*x^c5*exp(c6*t)`): Setting c5=1 gives `c4*x*exp(c6*t)`, which still can't equal `x*t`.

Going through all 51 candidates: Every single one uses exponential, trigonometric, or no t-dependence. None have a polynomial (linear) dependence on t multiplied by x.

Therefore, **no candidate can exactly match the GT**.
